This function is case-sensitive.</p><p>This function is useful for identifying similar strings; a smaller <a href="bit-functions#bithammingdistance">Hamming Distance</a> between two <code>simhashes</code> indicates greater similarity between the original strings.</p><h3 id="syntax" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Syntax<a class="headerlink" href="#syntax" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">wordShingleSimHashUTF8(string[, shinglesize])
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h3 id="arguments" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Arguments<a class="headerlink" href="#arguments" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><ul><li><code>string</code>: The UTF-8 string to process. <a href="../data-types/string">String</a>.</li><li><code>shinglesize</code>: The number of words in each shingle. Optional. Valid values are <code>1</code> to <code>25</code>. Default is <code>3</code>. <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt8</a>.</li></ul><h3 id="returns" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Returns<a class="headerlink" href="#returns" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>A 64-bit hash value. <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt64</a>.</p><h3 id="example" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Example<a class="headerlink" href="#example" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">SELECT wordShingleSimHashUTF8(&#x27;Bazinga® is a column-oriented database management system (DBMS) for online analytical processing of queries (OLAP).&#x27;) AS Hash

It returns a tuple containing these two hashes and is case-sensitive.</p><p>This function is useful for detecting semi-duplicate strings. If one of the returned hashes is identical for two strings, it suggests a high degree of similarity.</p><h3 id="syntax" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Syntax<a class="headerlink" href="#syntax" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">ngramMinHash(string[, ngramsize, hashnum])

It returns a tuple containing these two hashes.</p><p>This function is useful for detecting semi-duplicate strings. If one of the returned hashes is identical for two strings, it suggests a high degree of similarity.</p><h3 id="syntax" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Syntax<a class="headerlink" href="#syntax" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">ngramMinHashCaseInsensitiveUTF8(string [, ngramsize, hashnum])
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h3 id="arguments" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Arguments<a class="headerlink" href="#arguments" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><ul><li><code>string</code>: The UTF-8 string to process. <a href="../data-types/string">String</a>.</li><li><code>ngramsize</code>: The length of each n-gram. Optional. Valid values are <code>1</code> to <code>25</code>. Default is <code>3</code>. <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt8</a>.</li><li><code>hashnum</code>: The number of minimum and maximum hashes to use. Optional. Valid values are <code>1</code> to <code>25</code>. Default is <code>6</code>. <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt8</a>.</li></ul><h3 id="returns" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Returns<a class="headerlink" href="#returns" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>A <a href="../data-types/tuple">tuple</a> containing two <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt64</a> hash values (minimum and maximum). <a href="../data-types/tuple">Tuple</a>(<a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt64</a>, <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt64</a>).</p><h3 id="example" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Example<a class="headerlink" href="#example" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">SELECT ngramMinHashCaseInsensitiveUTF8(&#x27;Bazinga&#x27;) AS Tuple

This function is case-sensitive.</p><h3 id="syntax" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Syntax<a class="headerlink" href="#syntax" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">ngramMinHashArg(string[, ngramsize, hashnum])
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h3 id="arguments" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Arguments<a class="headerlink" href="#arguments" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><ul><li><code>string</code>: The ASCII string to process. <a href="../data-types/string">String</a>.</li><li><code>ngramsize</code>: The length of each n-gram. This function is case-sensitive.</p><h3 id="syntax" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Syntax<a class="headerlink" href="#syntax" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">ngramMinHashArgUTF8(string[, ngramsize, hashnum])
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h3 id="arguments" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Arguments<a class="headerlink" href="#arguments" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><ul><li><code>string</code>: The UTF-8 string to process. <a href="../data-types/string">String</a>.</li><li><code>ngramsize</code>: The length of each n-gram. Optional. Valid values are <code>1</code> to <code>25</code>. Default is <code>3</code>. <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt8</a>.</li><li><code>hashnum</code>: The number of minimum and maximum hashes to use. Optional. Valid values are <code>1</code> to <code>25</code>. Default is <code>6</code>. <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt8</a>.</li></ul><h3 id="returns" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Returns<a class="headerlink" href="#returns" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>A <a href="../data-types/tuple">tuple</a> containing two <a href="../data-types/tuple">tuples</a> of <a href="../data-types/string">strings</a>, representing the <code>hashnum</code> n-grams with the minimum and maximum hash values. <a href="../data-types/tuple">Tuple</a>(<a href="../data-types/tuple">Tuple</a>(<a href="../data-types/string">String</a>), <a href="../data-types/tuple">Tuple</a>(<a href="../data-types/string">String</a>)).</p><h3 id="example" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Example<a class="headerlink" href="#example" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">SELECT ngramMinHashArgUTF8(&#x27;Bazinga&#x27;) AS Tuple

It returns a tuple containing these two hashes and is case-sensitive.</p><p>This function is useful for detecting semi-duplicate strings. If one of the returned hashes is identical for two strings, it suggests a high degree of similarity.</p><h3 id="syntax" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Syntax<a class="headerlink" href="#syntax" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">wordShingleMinHash(string[, shinglesize, hashnum])
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h3 id="arguments" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Arguments<a class="headerlink" href="#arguments" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><ul><li><code>string</code>: The ASCII string to process. <a href="../data-types/string">String</a>.</li><li><code>shinglesize</code>: The number of words in each shingle. Optional. Valid values are <code>1</code> to <code>25</code>. Default is <code>3</code>. <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt8</a>.</li><li><code>hashnum</code>: The number of minimum and maximum hashes to use. Optional. Valid values are <code>1</code> to <code>25</code>. Default is <code>6</code>. <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt8</a>.</li></ul><h3 id="returns" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Returns<a class="headerlink" href="#returns" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>A <a href="../data-types/tuple">tuple</a> containing two <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt64</a> hash values (minimum and maximum). <a href="../data-types/tuple">Tuple</a>(<a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt64</a>, <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt64</a>).</p><h3 id="example" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Example<a class="headerlink" href="#example" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">SELECT wordShingleMinHash(&#x27;Bazinga® is a column-oriented database management system (DBMS) for online analytical processing of queries (OLAP).&#x27;) AS Tuple
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>Result:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">┌─Tuple──────────────────────────────────────┐
│ (16452112859864147620,5844417301642981317) │
└────────────────────────────────────────────┘
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h2 id="wordshingleminhashcaseinsensitive" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">wordShingleMinHashCaseInsensitive<a class="headerlink" href="#wordshingleminhashcaseinsensitive" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>Splits an ASCII string into word shingles and calculates minimum and maximum hash values for these shingles, ignoring case. It returns a tuple containing these two hashes.</p><p>This function is useful for detecting semi-duplicate strings. If one of the returned hashes is identical for two strings, it suggests a high degree of similarity.</p><h3 id="syntax" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Syntax<a class="headerlink" href="#syntax" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">wordShingleMinHashCaseInsensitive(string[, shinglesize, hashnum])
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h3 id="arguments" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Arguments<a class="headerlink" href="#arguments" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><ul><li><code>string</code>: The ASCII string to process. <a href="../data-types/string">String</a>.</li><li><code>shinglesize</code>: The number of words in each shingle. Optional. Valid values are <code>1</code> to <code>25</code>. Default is <code>3</code>. <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt8</a>.</li><li><code>hashnum</code>: The number of minimum and maximum hashes to use. Optional. Default is <code>6</code>. <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt8</a>.</li></ul><h3 id="returns" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Returns<a class="headerlink" href="#returns" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>A <a href="../data-types/tuple">tuple</a> containing two <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt64</a> hash values (minimum and maximum). <a href="../data-types/tuple">Tuple</a>(<a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt64</a>, <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt64</a>).</p><h3 id="example" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Example<a class="headerlink" href="#example" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">SELECT wordShingleMinHashCaseInsensitive(&#x27;Bazinga® is a column-oriented database management system (DBMS) for online analytical processing of queries (OLAP).&#x27;) AS Tuple

It returns a tuple containing these two hashes and is case-sensitive.</p><p>This function is useful for detecting semi-duplicate strings. If one of the returned hashes is identical for two strings, it suggests a high degree of similarity.</p><h3 id="syntax" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Syntax<a class="headerlink" href="#syntax" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">wordShingleMinHashUTF8(string[, shinglesize, hashnum])

This function is case-sensitive.</p><h3 id="syntax" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Syntax<a class="headerlink" href="#syntax" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">wordShingleMinHashArg(string[, shinglesize, hashnum])
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h3 id="arguments" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Arguments<a class="headerlink" href="#arguments" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><ul><li><code>string</code>: The ASCII string to process. <a href="../data-types/string">String</a>.</li><li><code>shinglesize</code>: The number of words in each shingle. Optional. Valid values are <code>1</code> to <code>25</code>. Default is <code>3</code>. <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt8</a>.</li><li><code>hashnum</code>: The number of minimum and maximum hashes to use. Optional. Valid values are <code>1</code> to <code>25</code>. Default is <code>6</code>. <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt8</a>.</li></ul><h3 id="returns" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Returns<a class="headerlink" href="#returns" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>A <a href="../data-types/tuple">tuple</a> containing two <a href="../data-types/tuple">tuples</a> of <a href="../data-types/string">strings</a>, representing the <code>hashnum</code> word shingles with the minimum and maximum hash values. <a href="../data-types/tuple">Tuple</a>(<a href="../data-types/tuple">Tuple</a>(<a href="../data-types/string">String</a>), <a href="../data-types/tuple">Tuple</a>(<a href="../data-types/string">String</a>)).</p><h3 id="example" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Example<a class="headerlink" href="#example" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">SELECT wordShingleMinHashArg(&#x27;Bazinga® is a column-oriented database management system (DBMS) for online analytical processing of queries (OLAP).&#x27;, 1, 3) AS Tuple

</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h3 id="arguments" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Arguments<a class="headerlink" href="#arguments" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><ul><li><code>string</code>: The UTF-8 string to process. <a href="../data-types/string">String</a>.</li><li><code>shinglesize</code>: The number of words in each shingle. Optional. Valid values are <code>1</code> to <code>25</code>. Default is <code>3</code>. <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt8</a>.</li><li><code>hashnum</code>: The number of minimum and maximum hashes to use. Optional. Valid values are <code>1</code> to <code>25</code>. Default is <code>6</code>. <a href="../data-types/int-uint">UInt8</a>.</li></ul><h3 id="returns" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Returns<a class="headerlink" href="#returns" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>A <a href="../data-types/tuple">tuple</a> containing two <a href="../data-types/tuple">tuples</a> of <a href="../data-types/string">strings</a>, representing the <code>hashnum</code> word shingles with the minimum and maximum hash values. <a href="../data-types/tuple">Tuple</a>(<a href="../data-types/tuple">Tuple</a>(<a href="../data-types/string">String</a>), <a href="../data-types/tuple">Tuple</a>(<a href="../data-types/string">String</a>)).</p><h3 id="example" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Example<a class="headerlink" href="#example" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">SELECT wordShingleMinHashArgCaseInsensitiveUTF8(&#x27;Bazinga® is a column-oriented database management system (DBMS) for online analytical processing of queries (OLAP).&#x27;, 1, 3) AS Tuple
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>Result:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">┌─Tuple──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

The generated IDs are reversible, meaning they can be decoded back to the original numbers.<!-- --> <!-- -->Alias: <code>sqid</code></p><h3 id="syntax" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Syntax<a class="headerlink" href="#syntax" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">sqidEncode(number1, ...)

2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 If the input string is not a valid Sqid, it returns an empty array.</p><h3 id="syntax" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Syntax<a class="headerlink" href="#syntax" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">sqidDecode(sqid)

1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h3 id="arguments" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Arguments<a class="headerlink" href="#arguments" │ [1,2,3,4,5]              │
└──────────────────────────┘
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h2 id="keccak256" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">keccak256<a class="headerlink" href="#keccak256" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>Calculates the Keccak-256 hash of a string input. This cryptographic hash function is widely used in EVM-based blockchain technologies.</p><h3 id="syntax" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Syntax<a class="headerlink" href="#syntax" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">keccak256(&#x27;s&#x27;)
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h3 id="arguments" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Arguments<a class="headerlink" href="#arguments" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><ul><li><code>s</code>: The input string for Keccak-256 hash calculation. <a href="../data-types/string">String</a>.</li></ul><h3 id="returns" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Returns<a class="headerlink" href="#returns" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>The Keccak-256 hash as a byte array. <a href="../data-types/fixedstring">FixedString(32)</a>.</p><h3 id="example" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Example<a class="headerlink" href="#example" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>Use the <a href="encoding-functions#hex">hex</a> function to format the result as a hex-encoded string.</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">SELECT hex(keccak256(&#x27;hello&#x27;))
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>Result:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">┌─hex(keccak256(&#x27;hello&#x27;))──────────────────────────────────────────┐

Hash Functions reference\nmeta:\n    description: Functions for hashing data.\nheadingMaxLevels: 2\n---\n\n# Hash functions\n\nHash functions are used to generate a fixed-size output (a hash value) from input data. They are often used for data integrity checks, unique identification, or distributing data across buckets.\n\n`Simhash` is a specific type of hash function that produces similar hash values for similar input arguments, useful for detecting near-duplicate content.\n\nMost hash functions in Tinybird can accept multiple arguments of various data types.\n\n{% callout type=\"info\" %}\nA hash of `NULL` is `NULL`. To generate a non-`NULL` hash for a `Nullable` column, wrap the column in a [tuple](../data-types/tuple):\n\n```sql\nSELECT cityHash64(tuple(NULL))\n```\n{% /callout %}\n\n## halfMD5\n\nThis function processes all input parameters as strings, computes their MD5 hash, and then combines these hashes. It extracts the first 8 bytes of the resulting hash and interprets them as a `UInt64` value in big-endian order.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nhalfMD5(par1, ...)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `par1, ...`: A variable number of input parameters of any [supported data type](../data-types/string). These are implicitly converted to strings for hashing.\n\n### Returns\n\nA 64-bit hash value. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT halfMD5(array('e','x','a'), 'mple', 10, toDateTime('2019-06-15 23:00:00')) AS halfMD5hash, toTypeName(halfMD5hash) AS type\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌────────halfMD5hash─┬─type───┐\n│ 186182704141653334 │ UInt64 │\n└────────────────────┴────────┘\n```\n\n## MD4\n\nCalculates the MD4 hash of a string input.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nMD4(input_string)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `input_string`: The string to hash. [String](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 128-bit MD4 hash value. [FixedString(16)](../data-types/fixedstring).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT MD4('Tinybird') AS md4_hash\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─md4_hash─────────┐\n│ 0000000000000000 │\n└──────────────────┘\n```\n\n## MD5\n\nCalculates the MD5 hash of a string input.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nMD5(input_string)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `input_string`: The string to hash. [String](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 128-bit MD5 hash value. [FixedString(16)](../data-types/fixedstring).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT MD5('Tinybird') AS md5_hash\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─md5_hash─────────┐\n│ 0000000000000000 │\n└──────────────────┘\n```\n\n## RIPEMD160\n\nGenerates a RIPEMD-160 hash value from a given string.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nRIPEMD160(input)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `input`: The string to hash. [String](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 160-bit RIPEMD-160 hash value. [FixedString(20)](../data-types/fixedstring).\n\n### Example\n\nUse the [hex](encoding-functions#hex) function to represent the result as a hex-encoded string.\n\n```sql\nSELECT HEX(RIPEMD160('The quick brown fox jumps over the lazy dog'))\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─HEX(RIPEMD160('The quick brown fox jumps over the lazy dog'))─┐\n│ 37F332F68DB77BD9D7EDD4969571AD671CF9DD3B                      │\n└───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## sipHash64\n\nComputes a 64-bit SipHash value for one or more input parameters. This cryptographic hash function is generally faster than MD5.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nsipHash64(par1,...)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `par1, ...`: A variable number of input parameters of any [supported data type](../data-types/string). These are implicitly converted to strings for hashing.\n\n### Returns\n\nA 64-bit hash value. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT sipHash64(array('e','x','a'), 'mple', 10, toDateTime('2019-06-15 23:00:00')) AS SipHash, toTypeName(SipHash) AS type\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌──────────────SipHash─┬─type───┐\n│ 11400366955626497465 │ UInt64 │\n└──────────────────────┴────────┘\n```\n\n## sipHash64Keyed\n\nCalculates a 64-bit SipHash value using an explicitly provided key, similar to `sipHash64`.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nsipHash64Keyed((k0, k1), par1,...)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `(k0, k1)`: A [tuple](../data-types/tuple) of two [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint) values that serve as the cryptographic key.\n- `par1, ...`: A variable number of input parameters of any [supported data type](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 64-bit hash value. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT sipHash64Keyed((506097522914230528, 1084818905618843912), array('e','x','a'), 'mple', 10, toDateTime('2019-06-15 23:00:00')) AS SipHash, toTypeName(SipHash) AS type\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─────────────SipHash─┬─type───┐\n│ 8017656310194184311 │ UInt64 │\n└─────────────────────┴────────┘\n```\n\n## sipHash128\n\nGenerates a 128-bit SipHash value, extending the 64-bit version by performing a 128-bit XOR folding of the final state.\n\n{% callout type=\"info\" %}\nThis 128-bit variant differs from the reference implementation and is considered weaker. For new projects, `sipHash128Reference` is generally recommended.\n{% /callout %}\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nsipHash128(par1,...)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `par1, ...`: A variable number of input parameters of any [supported data type](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 128-bit SipHash value. [FixedString(16)](../data-types/fixedstring).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT hex(sipHash128('foo', '\\x01', 3))\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─hex(sipHash128('foo', '', 3))────┐\n│ 9DE516A64A414D4B1B609415E4523F24 │\n└──────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## sipHash128Keyed\n\nCalculates a 128-bit SipHash value using an explicit key, similar to `sipHash128`.\n\n{% callout type=\"info\" %}\nThis 128-bit variant differs from the reference implementation and is considered weaker. For new projects, `sipHash128ReferenceKeyed` is generally recommended.\n{% /callout %}\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nsipHash128Keyed((k0, k1), par1,...)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `(k0, k1)`: A [tuple](../data-types/tuple) of two [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint) values that serve as the cryptographic key.\n- `par1, ...`: A variable number of input parameters of any [supported data type](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 128-bit SipHash value. [FixedString(16)](../data-types/fixedstring).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT hex(sipHash128Keyed((506097522914230528, 1084818905618843912),'foo', '\\x01', 3))\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─hex(sipHash128Keyed((506097522914230528, 1084818905618843912), 'foo', '', 3))─┐\n│ B8467F65C8B4CFD9A5F8BD733917D9BF                                              │\n└───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## sipHash128Reference\n\nGenerates a 128-bit SipHash value using the official 128-bit algorithm from the original authors of SipHash.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nsipHash128Reference(par1,...)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `par1, ...`: A variable number of input parameters of any [supported data type](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 128-bit SipHash value. [FixedString(16)](../data-types/fixedstring).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT hex(sipHash128Reference('foo', '\\x01', 3))\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─hex(sipHash128Reference('foo', '', 3))─┐\n│ 4D1BE1A22D7F5933C0873E1698426260       │\n└────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## sipHash128ReferenceKeyed\n\nCalculates a 128-bit SipHash value using the official reference algorithm and an explicitly provided key.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nsipHash128ReferenceKeyed((k0, k1), par1,...)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `(k0, k1)`: A [tuple](../data-types/tuple) of two [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint) values that serve as the cryptographic key.\n- `par1, ...`: A variable number of input parameters of any [supported data type](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 128-bit SipHash value. [FixedString(16)](../data-types/fixedstring).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT hex(sipHash128ReferenceKeyed((506097522914230528, 1084818905618843912),'foo', '\\x01', 3))\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─hex(sipHash128ReferenceKeyed((506097522914230528, 1084818905618843912), 'foo', '', 3))─┐\n│ 630133C9722DC08646156B8130C4CDC8                                                       │\n└────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## cityHash64\n\nProduces a 64-bit CityHash value, a fast non-cryptographic hash function. It uses the CityHash algorithm for string inputs and a specific non-cryptographic hash for other data types, combining results with the CityHash combinator.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\ncityHash64(par1,...)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `par1, ...`: A variable number of input parameters of any [supported data type](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 64-bit hash value. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT cityHash64(array('e','x','a'), 'mple', 10, toDateTime('2019-06-15 23:00:00')) AS CityHash, toTypeName(CityHash) AS type\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─────────────CityHash─┬─type───┐\n│ 12072650598913549138 │ UInt64 │\n└──────────────────────┴────────┘\n```\n\n## intHash32\n\nCalculates a 32-bit hash code from any integer input. This is a relatively fast, non-cryptographic hash function suitable for numbers.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nintHash32(int)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `int`: The integer value to hash. [(U)Int*](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 32-bit hash code. [UInt32](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT intHash32(42)\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─intHash32(42)─┐\n│    1228623923 │\n└───────────────┘\n```\n\n## intHash64\n\nCalculates a 64-bit hash code from any integer input. This non-cryptographic hash function is faster than `intHash32` and provides a higher quality hash for numbers.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nintHash64(int)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `int`: The integer value to hash. [(U)Int*](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 64-bit hash code. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT intHash64(42)\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌────────intHash64(42)─┐\n│ 11490350930367293593 │\n└──────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## SHA1, SHA224, SHA256, SHA512, SHA512_256\n\nThese functions compute various SHA (Secure Hash Algorithm) hashes (SHA-1, SHA-224, SHA-256, SHA-512, SHA-512/256) from a string input.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nSHA1('s')\nSHA224('s')\nSHA256('s')\nSHA512('s')\nSHA512_256('s')\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `s`: The input string for SHA hash calculation. [String](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nThe SHA hash as a hex-unencoded [FixedString](../data-types/fixedstring).\n- `SHA1`: [FixedString(20)](../data-types/fixedstring)\n- `SHA224`: [FixedString(28)](../data-types/fixedstring)\n- `SHA256`: [FixedString(32)](../data-types/fixedstring)\n- `SHA512`: [FixedString(64)](../data-types/fixedstring)\n- `SHA512_256`: [FixedString(32)](../data-types/fixedstring)\n\n### Example\n\nUse the [hex](encoding-functions#hex) function to represent the result as a hex-encoded string.\n\n```sql\nSELECT hex(SHA1('abc'))\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─hex(SHA1('abc'))─────────────────────────┐\n│ A9993E364706816ABA3E25717850C26C9CD0D89D │\n└──────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## BLAKE3\n\nCalculates the BLAKE3 hash of a string input. This cryptographic hash function is known for its speed, offering performance approximately twice as fast as SHA-2 while producing hashes of the same length as SHA-256.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nBLAKE3('s')\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `s`: The input string for BLAKE3 hash calculation. [String](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nThe BLAKE3 hash as a byte array. [FixedString(32)](../data-types/fixedstring).\n\n### Example\n\nUse the [hex](encoding-functions#hex) function to represent the result as a hex-encoded string.\n\n```sql\nSELECT hex(BLAKE3('ABC'))\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─hex(BLAKE3('ABC'))───────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ D1717274597CF0289694F75D96D444B992A096F1AFD8E7BBFA6EBB1D360FEDFC │\n└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## URLHash(url[, N])\n\nThis function computes a fast, non-cryptographic hash for a URL string after applying some normalization. It can hash the entire URL or up to a specified level in its hierarchy.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nURLHash(url)\nURLHash(url, N)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `url`: The URL string to hash. [String](../data-types/string).\n- `N`: An optional integer specifying the URL hierarchy level up to which the hash should be calculated. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Returns\n\nA hash value. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT URLHash('https://tinybird.co/docs/sql-reference/functions/hash-functions') AS full_url_hash,\n       URLHash('https://tinybird.co/docs/sql-reference/functions/hash-functions', 2) AS level_2_hash\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─full_url_hash──────┬─level_2_hash───────┐\n│ 123456789012345678 │ 987654321098765432 │\n└────────────────────┴────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## farmFingerprint64\n\nThis function computes a 64-bit Fingerprint value using the FarmHash algorithm. It is recommended for generating stable and portable hash values.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nfarmFingerprint64(par1, ...)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `par1, ...`: A variable number of input parameters of any [supported data type](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 64-bit hash value. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT farmFingerprint64('Tinybird') AS fingerprint_hash\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─fingerprint_hash───┐\n│ 123456789012345678 │\n└────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## farmHash64\n\nThis function computes a 64-bit hash value using the FarmHash algorithm.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nfarmHash64(par1, ...)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `par1, ...`: A variable number of input parameters of any [supported data type](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 64-bit hash value. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT farmHash64(array('e','x','a'), 'mple', 10, toDateTime('2019-06-15 23:00:00')) AS FarmHash, toTypeName(FarmHash) AS type\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─────────────FarmHash─┬─type───┐\n│ 17790458267262532859 │ UInt64 │\n└──────────────────────┴────────┘\n```\n\n## javaHash\n\nCalculates a hash value compatible with Java's `hashCode()` method for strings, bytes, shorts, integers, and longs. This function is primarily useful for compatibility with existing Java systems rather than for high-quality or fast hashing.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\njavaHash(value)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `value`: The input value to hash. Can be a [String](../data-types/string) or an integer type.\n\n### Returns\n\nA 32-bit signed integer hash value. [Int32](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT javaHash(toInt32(123))\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─javaHash(toInt32(123))─┐\n│               123      │\n└────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n```sql\nSELECT javaHash('Hello, world!')\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─javaHash('Hello, world!')─┐\n│               -1880044555 │\n└───────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## javaHashUTF16LE\n\nCalculates a Java-compatible hash value for a string, assuming the input string is encoded in UTF-16LE.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\njavaHashUTF16LE(stringUtf16le)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `stringUtf16le`: A string encoded in UTF-16LE. [String](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 32-bit signed integer hash value. [Int32](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT javaHashUTF16LE(convertCharset('test', 'utf-8', 'utf-16le'))\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─javaHashUTF16LE(convertCharset('test', 'utf-8', 'utf-16le'))─┐\n│                                                      3556498 │\n└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## hiveHash\n\nCalculates a hash value compatible with Apache Hive versions prior to 3.0. This function is essentially `javaHash` with the sign bit zeroed out, and is primarily used for compatibility with existing Hive systems.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nhiveHash(value)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `value`: The input value to hash. [String](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 32-bit signed integer hash value. [Int32](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT hiveHash('Hello, world!')\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─hiveHash('Hello, world!')─┐\n│                 267439093 │\n└───────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## metroHash64\n\nProduces a 64-bit MetroHash value, a fast non-cryptographic hash function.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nmetroHash64(par1, ...)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `par1, ...`: A variable number of input parameters of any [supported data type](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 64-bit hash value. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT metroHash64(array('e','x','a'), 'mple', 10, toDateTime('2019-06-15 23:00:00')) AS MetroHash, toTypeName(MetroHash) AS type\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌────────────MetroHash─┬─type───┐\n│ 14235658766382344533 │ UInt64 │\n└──────────────────────┴────────┘\n```\n\n## jumpConsistentHash\n\nCalculates a Jump Consistent Hash for a given key and number of buckets. This algorithm provides a simple and fast way to assign keys to buckets in a consistent manner.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\njumpConsistentHash(key, num_buckets)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `key`: A 64-bit unsigned integer key. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n- `num_buckets`: The number of available buckets. [Int32](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Returns\n\nThe assigned bucket index. [Int32](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT jumpConsistentHash(1234567890123456789, 100) AS bucket_id\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─bucket_id─┐\n│        42 │\n└───────────┘\n```\n\n## kostikConsistentHash\n\nThis function implements an O(1) time and space consistent hashing algorithm. It efficiently distributes keys among a fixed number of buckets.\nAlias: `yandexConsistentHash`\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nkostikConsistentHash(input, n)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `input`: A 64-bit unsigned integer key. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n- `n`: The number of buckets. [UInt16](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 16-bit unsigned integer hash value representing the assigned bucket. [UInt16](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT kostikConsistentHash(16045690984833335023, 2)\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─kostikConsistentHash(16045690984833335023, 2)─┐\n│                                             1 │\n└───────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## murmurHash2_32, murmurHash2_64\n\nThese functions produce 32-bit or 64-bit MurmurHash2 values, which are fast, non-cryptographic hash functions suitable for general-purpose hashing.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nmurmurHash2_32(par1, ...)\nmurmurHash2_64(par1, ...)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `par1, ...`: A variable number of input parameters of any [supported data type](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\n- `murmurHash2_32`: A 32-bit hash value. [UInt32](../data-types/int-uint).\n- `murmurHash2_64`: A 64-bit hash value. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT murmurHash2_64(array('e','x','a'), 'mple', 10, toDateTime('2019-06-15 23:00:00')) AS MurmurHash2, toTypeName(MurmurHash2) AS type\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌──────────MurmurHash2─┬─type───┐\n│ 11832096901709403633 │ UInt64 │\n└──────────────────────┴────────┘\n```\n\n## gccMurmurHash\n\nCalculates a 64-bit MurmurHash2 value using the same hash seed as GCC's standard library. This ensures portability of hash results between different compilers like Clang and GCC.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\ngccMurmurHash(par1, ...)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `par1, ...`: A variable number of parameters of any [supported data type](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 64-bit hash value. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT\n    gccMurmurHash(1, 2, 3) AS res1,\n    gccMurmurHash(('a', [1, 2, 3], 4, (4, ['foo', 'bar'], 1, (1, 2)))) AS res2\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─────────────────res1─┬────────────────res2─┐\n│ 12384823029245979431 │ 1188926775431157506 │\n└──────────────────────┴─────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## kafkaMurmurHash\n\nCalculates a 32-bit MurmurHash2 value, specifically designed to be compatible with Apache Kafka's default partitioner. It uses Kafka's hash seed and clears the highest bit of the result.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nkafkaMurmurHash(par1, ...)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `par1, ...`: A variable number of parameters of any [supported data type](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 32-bit hash value. [UInt32](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT\n    kafkaMurmurHash('foobar') AS res1,\n    kafkaMurmurHash(array('e','x','a'), 'mple', 10, toDateTime('2019-06-15 23:00:00')) AS res2\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌───────res1─┬─────res2─┐\n│ 1357151166 │ 85479775 │\n└────────────┴──────────┘\n```\n\n## murmurHash3_32, murmurHash3_64\n\nThese functions produce 32-bit or 64-bit MurmurHash3 values, which are fast, non-cryptographic hash functions offering improved collision resistance over MurmurHash2.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nmurmurHash3_32(par1, ...)\nmurmurHash3_64(par1, ...)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `par1, ...`: A variable number of input parameters of any [supported data type](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\n- `murmurHash3_32`: A 32-bit hash value. [UInt32](../data-types/int-uint).\n- `murmurHash3_64`: A 64-bit hash value. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT murmurHash3_32(array('e','x','a'), 'mple', 10, toDateTime('2019-06-15 23:00:00')) AS MurmurHash3, toTypeName(MurmurHash3) AS type\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─MurmurHash3─┬─type───┐\n│     2152717 │ UInt32 │\n└─────────────┴────────┘\n```\n\n## murmurHash3_128\n\nProduces a 128-bit MurmurHash3 value, providing a longer hash for increased uniqueness and reduced collision probability.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nmurmurHash3_128(expr)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `expr`: A list of expressions to hash. [String](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 128-bit MurmurHash3 hash value. [FixedString(16)](../data-types/fixedstring).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT hex(murmurHash3_128('foo', 'foo', 'foo'))\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─hex(murmurHash3_128('foo', 'foo', 'foo'))─┐\n│ F8F7AD9B6CD4CF117A71E277E2EC2931          │\n└───────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## xxh3\n\nProduces a 64-bit hash value using the xxh3 algorithm, known for its extreme speed and good hash quality.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nxxh3(expr)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `expr`: A list of expressions of any data type to hash.\n\n### Returns\n\nA 64-bit xxh3 hash value. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT xxh3('Hello', 'world')\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─xxh3('Hello', 'world')─┐\n│    5607458076371731292 │\n└────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## xxHash32, xxHash64\n\nThese functions calculate `xxHash` values from a string input, available in 32-bit and 64-bit versions. xxHash is a very fast non-cryptographic hash algorithm.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nxxHash32(input_string)\nxxHash64(input_string)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `input_string`: The string to hash. [String](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\n- `xxHash32`: A 32-bit hash value. [UInt32](../data-types/int-uint).\n- `xxHash64`: A 64-bit hash value. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n{% callout type=\"info\" %}\nThe return type will be `UInt32` for `xxHash32` and `UInt64` for `xxHash64`.\n{% /callout %}\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT xxHash32('Hello, world!')\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─xxHash32('Hello, world!')─┐\n│                 834093149 │\n└───────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## ngramSimHash\n\nSplits an ASCII string into n-grams (sequences of `ngramsize` symbols) and computes a `simhash` for these n-grams. This function is case-sensitive.\n\nThis function is useful for identifying similar strings; a smaller [Hamming Distance](bit-functions#bithammingdistance) between two `simhashes` indicates greater similarity between the original strings.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nngramSimHash(string[, ngramsize])\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `string`: The ASCII string to process. [String](../data-types/string).\n- `ngramsize`: The length of each n-gram. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `3`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 64-bit hash value. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT ngramSimHash('Bazinga') AS Hash\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌───────Hash─┐\n│ 1627567969 │\n└────────────┘\n```\n\n## ngramSimHashCaseInsensitive\n\nSplits an ASCII string into n-grams (sequences of `ngramsize` symbols) and computes a `simhash` for these n-grams, ignoring case.\n\nThis function is useful for identifying similar strings; a smaller [Hamming Distance](bit-functions#bithammingdistance) between two `simhashes` indicates greater similarity between the original strings.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nngramSimHashCaseInsensitive(string[, ngramsize])\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `string`: The ASCII string to process. [String](../data-types/string).\n- `ngramsize`: The length of each n-gram. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `3`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 64-bit hash value. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT ngramSimHashCaseInsensitive('Bazinga') AS Hash\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌──────Hash─┐\n│ 562180645 │\n└───────────┘\n```\n\n## ngramSimHashUTF8\n\nSplits a UTF-8 string into n-grams (sequences of `ngramsize` symbols) and computes a `simhash` for these n-grams. [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT wordShingleSimHash('Bazinga® is a column-oriented database management system (DBMS) for online analytical processing of queries (OLAP).') AS Hash\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌───────Hash─┐\n│ 2328277067 │\n└────────────┘\n```\n\n## wordShingleSimHashCaseInsensitive\n\nSplits an ASCII string into word shingles (sequences of `shinglesize` words) and computes a `simhash` for these shingles, ignoring case.\n\nThis function is useful for identifying similar strings; a smaller [Hamming Distance](bit-functions#bithammingdistance) between two `simhashes` indicates greater similarity between the original strings.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nwordShingleSimHashCaseInsensitive(string[, shinglesize])\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `string`: The ASCII string to process. [String](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nA 64-bit hash value. It returns a tuple containing these two hashes and is case-sensitive.\n\nThis function is useful for detecting semi-duplicate strings. If one of the returned hashes is identical for two strings, it suggests a high degree of similarity.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nngramMinHash(string[, ngramsize, hashnum])\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `string`: The ASCII string to process. [String](../data-types/string).\n- `ngramsize`: The length of each n-gram. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `3`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n- `hashnum`: The number of minimum and maximum hashes to use. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `6`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Returns\n\nA [tuple](../data-types/tuple) containing two [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint) hash values (minimum and maximum). [Tuple](../data-types/tuple)([UInt64](../data-types/int-uint), [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint)).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT ngramMinHash('Bazinga') AS Tuple\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─Tuple──────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ (18333312859352735453,9054248444481805918) │\n└────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## ngramMinHashCaseInsensitive\n\nSplits an ASCII string into n-grams and calculates minimum and maximum hash values for these n-grams, ignoring case. It returns a tuple containing these two hashes.\n\nThis function is useful for detecting semi-duplicate strings. If one of the returned hashes is identical for two strings, it suggests a high degree of similarity.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nngramMinHashCaseInsensitive(string[, ngramsize, hashnum])\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `string`: The ASCII string to process. [String](../data-types/string).\n- `ngramsize`: The length of each n-gram. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `3`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n- `hashnum`: The number of minimum and maximum hashes to use. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `6`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Returns\n\nA [tuple](../data-types/tuple) containing two [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint) hash values (minimum and maximum). [Tuple](../data-types/tuple)([UInt64](../data-types/int-uint), [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint)).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT ngramMinHashCaseInsensitive('Bazinga') AS Tuple\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─Tuple──────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ (2106263556442004574,13203602793651726206) │\n└────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## ngramMinHashUTF8\n\nSplits a UTF-8 string into n-grams and calculates minimum and maximum hash values for these n-grams. It returns a tuple containing these two hashes.\n\nThis function is useful for detecting semi-duplicate strings. If one of the returned hashes is identical for two strings, it suggests a high degree of similarity.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nngramMinHashCaseInsensitiveUTF8(string [, ngramsize, hashnum])\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `string`: The UTF-8 string to process. [String](../data-types/string).\n- `ngramsize`: The length of each n-gram. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `3`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n- `hashnum`: The number of minimum and maximum hashes to use. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `6`. [Tuple](../data-types/tuple)([UInt64](../data-types/int-uint), [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint)).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT ngramMinHashCaseInsensitiveUTF8('Bazinga') AS Tuple\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─Tuple───────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ (12493625717655877135,13203602793651726206) │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## ngramMinHashArg\n\nSplits an ASCII string into n-grams and returns the specific n-grams that correspond to the minimum and maximum hash values, as determined by `ngramMinHash`. This function is case-sensitive.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nngramMinHashArg(string[, ngramsize, hashnum])\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `string`: The ASCII string to process. [String](../data-types/string).\n- `ngramsize`: The length of each n-gram. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `3`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n- `hashnum`: The number of minimum and maximum hashes to use. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `6`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Returns\n\nA [tuple](../data-types/tuple) containing two [tuples](../data-types/tuple) of [strings](../data-types/string), representing the `hashnum` n-grams with the minimum and maximum hash values. [Tuple](../data-types/tuple)([Tuple](../data-types/tuple)([String](../data-types/string)), [Tuple](../data-types/tuple)([String](../data-types/string))).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT ngramMinHashArg('Bazinga') AS Tuple\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─Tuple─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ (('ous','ick','lic','Hou','kHo','use'),('Hou','lic','ick','ous','ckH','Cli')) │\n└───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## ngramMinHashArgCaseInsensitive\n\nSplits an ASCII string into n-grams and returns the specific n-grams that correspond to the minimum and maximum hash values, as determined by `ngramMinHashCaseInsensitive`, ignoring case.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nngramMinHashArgCaseInsensitive(string[, ngramsize, hashnum])\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `string`: The ASCII string to process. It returns a tuple containing these two hashes and is case-sensitive.\n\nThis function is useful for detecting semi-duplicate strings. If one of the returned hashes is identical for two strings, it suggests a high degree of similarity.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nwordShingleMinHashUTF8(string[, shinglesize, hashnum])\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `string`: The UTF-8 string to process. [String](../data-types/string).\n- `shinglesize`: The number of words in each shingle. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `3`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n- `hashnum`: The number of minimum and maximum hashes to use. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `6`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Returns\n\nA [tuple](../data-types/tuple) containing two [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint) hash values (minimum and maximum). [Tuple](../data-types/tuple)([UInt64](../data-types/int-uint), [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint)).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT wordShingleMinHashUTF8('Bazinga® is a column-oriented database management system (DBMS) for online analytical processing of queries (OLAP).') AS Tuple\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─Tuple──────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ (16452112859864147620,5844417301642981317) │\n└────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## wordShingleMinHashCaseInsensitiveUTF8\n\nSplits a UTF-8 string into word shingles and calculates minimum and maximum hash values for these shingles, ignoring case. It returns a tuple containing these two hashes.\n\nThis function is useful for detecting semi-duplicate strings. If one of the returned hashes is identical for two strings, it suggests a high degree of similarity.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nwordShingleMinHashCaseInsensitiveUTF8(string[, shinglesize, hashnum])\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `string`: The UTF-8 string to process. [String](../data-types/string).\n- `shinglesize`: The number of words in each shingle. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `3`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n- `hashnum`: The number of minimum and maximum hashes to use. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `6`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Returns\n\nA [tuple](../data-types/tuple) containing two [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint) hash values (minimum and maximum). [Tuple](../data-types/tuple)([UInt64](../data-types/int-uint), [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint)).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT wordShingleMinHashCaseInsensitiveUTF8('Bazinga® is a column-oriented database management system (DBMS) for online analytical processing of queries (OLAP).') AS Tuple\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─Tuple─────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ (3065874883688416519,1634050779997673240) │\n└───────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## wordShingleMinHashArg\n\nSplits an ASCII string into word shingles and returns the specific word shingles that correspond to the minimum and maximum hash values, as determined by `wordShingleMinHash`. This function is case-sensitive.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nwordShingleMinHashArg(string[, shinglesize, hashnum])\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `string`: The ASCII string to process. [String](../data-types/string).\n- `shinglesize`: The number of words in each shingle. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `3`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n- `hashnum`: The number of minimum and maximum hashes to use. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `6`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Returns\n\nA [tuple](../data-types/tuple) containing two [tuples](../data-types/tuple) of [strings](../data-types/string), representing the `hashnum` word shingles with the minimum and maximum hash values. [Tuple](../data-types/tuple)([Tuple](../data-types/tuple)([String](../data-types/string)), [Tuple](../data-types/tuple)([String](../data-types/string))).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT wordShingleMinHashArg('Bazinga® is a column-oriented database management system (DBMS) for online analytical processing of queries (OLAP).', 1, 3) AS Tuple\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─Tuple─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ (('OLAP','database','analytical'),('online','oriented','processing')) │\n└───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## wordShingleMinHashArgCaseInsensitive\n\nSplits an ASCII string into word shingles and returns the specific word shingles that correspond to the minimum and maximum hash values, as determined by `wordShingleMinHashCaseInsensitive`, ignoring case.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nwordShingleMinHashArgCaseInsensitive(string[, shinglesize, hashnum])\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `string`: The ASCII string to process. [String](../data-types/string).\n- `shinglesize`: The number of words in each shingle. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `3`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n- `hashnum`: The number of minimum and maximum hashes to use. Optional. Valid values are `1` to `25`. Default is `6`. [UInt8](../data-types/int-uint).\n\n### Returns\n\nA [tuple](../data-types/tuple) containing two [tuples](../data-types/tuple) of [strings](../data-types/string), representing the `hashnum` word shingles with the minimum and maximum hash values. [Tuple](../data-types/tuple)([Tuple](../data-types/tuple)([String](../data-types/string)), [Tuple](../data-types/tuple)([String](../data-types/string))).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT wordShingleMinHashArgCaseInsensitive('Bazinga® is a column-oriented database management system (DBMS) for online analytical processing of queries (OLAP).', 1, 3) AS Tuple\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─Tuple──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ (('queries','database','analytical'),('oriented','processing','DBMS')) │\n└────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## wordShingleMinHashArgUTF8\n\nSplits a UTF-8 string into word shingles and returns the specific word shingles that correspond to the minimum and maximum hash values, as determined by `wordShingleMinHashUTF8`. This function is case-sensitive.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nwordShingleMinHashArgUTF8(string[, shinglesize, hashnum])\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `string`: The UTF-8 string to process. The generated IDs are reversible, meaning they can be decoded back to the original numbers.\nAlias: `sqid`\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nsqidEncode(number1, ...)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `number1, ...`: A variable number of unsigned integer values ([UInt8](../data-types/int-uint), [UInt16](../data-types/int-uint), [UInt32](../data-types/int-uint), or [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint)).\n\n### Returns\n\nA Sqid [String](../data-types/string).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT sqidEncode(1, 2, 3, 4, 5)\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─sqidEncode(1, 2, 3, 4, 5)─┐\n│ gXHfJ1C6dN                │\n└───────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## sqidDecode\n\nDecodes a Sqid string back into its original sequence of numbers. If the input string is not a valid Sqid, it returns an empty array.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nsqidDecode(sqid)\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `sqid`: The Sqid string to decode. [String](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nAn [array](../data-types/array) of [UInt64](../data-types/int-uint) values representing the decoded numbers. [Array(UInt64)](../data-types/array).\n\n### Example\n\n```sql\nSELECT sqidDecode('gXHfJ1C6dN')\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─sqidDecode('gXHfJ1C6dN')─┐\n│ [1,2,3,4,5]              │\n└──────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## keccak256\n\nCalculates the Keccak-256 hash of a string input. This cryptographic hash function is widely used in EVM-based blockchain technologies.\n\n### Syntax\n\n```sql\nkeccak256('s')\n```\n\n### Arguments\n\n- `s`: The input string for Keccak-256 hash calculation. [String](../data-types/string).\n\n### Returns\n\nThe Keccak-256 hash as a byte array. [FixedString(32)](../data-types/fixedstring).\n\n### Example\n\nUse the [hex](encoding-functions#hex) function to format the result as a hex-encoded string.\n\n```sql\nSELECT hex(keccak256('hello'))\n```\n\nResult:\n\n```result\n┌─hex(keccak256('hello'))──────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ 1C8AFF950685C2ED4BC3174F3472287B56D9517B9C948127319A09A7A36DEAC8 │\n└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"38:{\"fill\":\"currentColor\",\"d\":\"M7.86 9.742a1 1 0 0 0-.08.1.5.5 0 0 0-.06.12.4.4 0 0 0-.04.12 1 1 0 0 0 0 .134.56.56 0 0 0 .053.253.6.6 0 0 0 .36.36.63.63 0 0 0 .507 0 .6.6 0 0 0 .36-.36.7.7 0 0 0 .04-.253.667.667 0 0 0-1.14-.474m.473-8.86a6.667 6.667 0 1 0 0 13.334 6.667 6.667 0 0 0 0-13.334m0 12a5.333 5.333 0 1 1 0-10.666 5.333 5.333 0 0 1 0 10.666m0-8.666a2 2 0 0 0-1.733 1 .667.667 0 1 0 1.153.666.667.667 0 0 1 1.052-.138.667.667 0 0 1-.472 1.138.667.667 0 0 0-.666.667v.667a.667.667 0 0 0 1.333 0v-.12a2 2 0 0 0-.667-3.88\"}\n37:[\"$\",\"path\",null,\"$38\"]\n"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"8:[\"$\",\"div\",null,{\"className\":\"relative max-w-7xl mx-auto px-5 md:px-6 xl:grid xl:grid-cols-[1fr_280px]\",\"children\":[[\"$\",\"div\",null,{\"className\":\"max-w-4xl text-body md:px-4 md:pb-20 relative\",\"role\":\"main\",\"children\":[[\"$\",\"$L20\",null,{\"pageContent\":\"$21\",\"pagePath\":\"app/__sql-reference/functions/hash-functions\",\"children\":[\"$\",\"article\",null,{\"children\":[[\"$\",\"$L22\",null,{\"level\":1,\"name\":\"Heading\",\"children\":\"Hash functions\"}],[\"$\",\"p\",null,{\"children\":\"Hash functions are used to generate a fixed-size output (a hash value) from input data.
